Spring and Autumn Annals

The Japanese Fear the Soviet Air Force 236

— Zhanlu

To shout the slogan "The Japanese fear the Soviet Air Force" in a crowded place, everyone would laugh their heads off. Would the Japanese fear the Soviet Air Force? If the Japanese were really afraid of the Soviet Air Force, then why did the people of Suzhou cry and scream in fear after the Japanese planes visited Wumen during the January 28th Incident, and why did they take their families away to avoid it? Ha ha! What lies are you telling?

The facts tell me that I'm not telling any lies. The Japanese do fear the Soviet Air Force, but this Soviet Air Force is not the soft-spoken, gentle Soviet Air Force, but the Soviet air force that flies over the heads of the Japanese. The seven characters "Soviet Air Force flies over the heads" are simplified into three characters, which is called the Soviet Air Force.

The Japanese have more than enough navy and army to deal with the Soviet Union, but their air force is dwarfed in comparison; this argument is often seen in Japanese newspapers, so it can be seen that the Japanese are not afraid of the Soviet sea and Soviet land, but only the Soviet Air Force. The Soviet Union saw through the Japanese fear, so the Far East Affairs Bureau issued a declaration, stating: "When the Japanese start aggression in the Far East, the Soviet Air Force is ready to resolve the most densely populated central areas of the enemy." The momentum of the Soviet Air Force is so strong that even if the Japanese are bold, they should have considerable fear.

This is not the Soviet Union bluffing. British female journalist Mrs. Trulamon also wrote an article saying: "The Soviet Union has an advantage in air force attacks on Japan; only because the development of the Soviet Air Force has made rapid progress in recent years, exceeding the Japanese. The shortest distance between the Soviet coastal state and Japan is only 350 miles, and it is more than enough to send the air force to attack Japan. If the Soviet Air Force uses four long-range motorized-equipped aircraft to carry out air strikes on Japanese cities from its base in Vladivostok, it would be more than enough." The arguments of foreigners are like this, so it can be seen that the Soviet Air Force really has a force that cannot be underestimated.

There is a very possible war between Japan and Russia; however, the first bullet must be fired by the Japanese, and it is afraid that it will not become a fact. Why? Because "the Japanese fear the Soviet Air Force."

Street Scene After the Rain 237

— 愼言

Life is inherently full of troubles, but looking at the dictionary, in the "heart" radical, nine out of ten characters are adjectives describing worry and sorrow. From this, one can imagine! Because of this understanding, I believe with utmost sincerity that the sighs of those gentlemen who have eaten their fill of Western cuisine and sit on flushing toilets smoking cigars are also expressions of the same "life is inherently full of troubles." However, the troubles and anxieties of these gentlemen are ultimately one-sided, belonging only to the realm of the spiritual. At most, they are merely quarreling over family issues, love affairs, or matters of face. But for us poor folks, it's different. Spiritual troubles are, of course, unavoidable, and there's no need to elaborate on that here. Let me talk about the suffering the poor endure due to material lack.

Take the most obvious example: the street after the rain. After the rain, while the gentlemen are dressed in elegant, lightweight clothes, sitting in their brand-new automobiles or rented carriages, speeding across the smooth asphalt roads, the poor are relying on their meager material resources to fight the wind and rain on the muddy sidewalks. Those who wear raincoats, carry umbrellas, and desperately try to squeeze into the tram are considered the upper class of the poor. Next are those who have some rain gear but can't afford the fare. Then, there are those that the gentlemen cannot imagine. They have never worn leather shoes. When it rains, they go barefoot. They have never worn raincoats. When it rains, they can only use their body temperature as their sole defense against the rain. Besides that, they still have to run, sweat, and work as usual in the wind and rain.

When you pass by those less bustling streets after the rain – around seven or eight o'clock in the evening – your first impression is inevitably those newsboys with bare calves, wearing very tattered and dirty old clothes. Whenever a tram or bus arrives at the station, they rush out from the rain and darkness, shouting "Late Night News," "Great American Evening News" in extremely desolate tones. When the vehicle drives away, they shrink back into the darkness where they can shelter from the rain. They wipe the raindrops from their heads with their sleeves, and anxiously count the newspapers in their hands or the copper coins in their pockets, secretly worrying that the rain will ruin their sales.

Friend, do you have children at home? If you do, and you love them very much, then I hope you never meet these poor little souls on the streets after the rain! Because I believe that most people's hearts are made of flesh?

Tragedy 238

— Yan Chonglou

I often see news in the papers about cars running over pedestrians, and sometimes I even witness people lying bloody after being hit by cars. But this time, it happened to me.

The story is this: The day before yesterday, I left home, preparing to take the bus to work. But before I could get on the bus, it started moving. My hand slipped, and the wheel ran over my leg. "This time my leg is broken! …But there are still so many things waiting for me to do!…" In the instant when one of my legs completely lost sensation, that's what I was thinking.

The heavy wheel weighing a thousand pounds ran over my left leg. I quickly supported myself with my right leg. I checked to see if my crushed leg was still there. I really couldn’t understand how it could still be there after such high pressure.

But the left leg was showing a very serious injury! I struggled to get on the bus that ran me over, avoiding the gazes of the spectators who were watching as if it were a show.

I didn't blame the "ticket seller" and "driver" who injured me. So they complimented me as a "tough guy" and "strong one." They said it was unprecedented for someone like me to remain so calm after being run over by a wheel.

After arriving at the doctor's and being bandaged up, the injury gradually began to hurt! At this moment, I deeply believed in the saying: "The road is like a tiger's mouth, pedestrians have no safety!"

Recently, I just finished writing a novel called "Tragedy in Loneliness," but I never expected that I myself would encounter this tragic scene in quick succession.

Sketches of the Return Voyage (Part 1) 241

— Huang Kangtun

Life in the South Seas

Having lived in the South Seas for six consecutive years, from Penang in the British Straits Settlements to Rangoon, to Medan on Dutch Sumatra; it was only one long "endless summer." In the tropics, there are no distinct seasons, and it is green all year round.

Looking at the vast coconut groves, orderly rubber plantations, verdant mountains, and lush green sea, the scent of bananas and the taste of durian are enough to intoxicate. The wide, smooth roads, well-maintained cities, towering golden pagodas, the domed Muslim mosques marked with a crescent, and the cube-shaped "red-haired buildings" with red tiles and green windows – all the static objects of new architecture are enough to make one envious. The dark, strong, and uninhibited "coolies" who live under the sky are enough to evoke pity. The natives who use their right hand as a knife and fork, and their left hand to wipe themselves and fall asleep, completely forgetting the world, are enough to evoke compassion. The "big bosses" who enjoy luxury and forget their ancestors are enough to evoke inner numbness. The innocent and naive overseas Chinese students who can speak several dialects are enough to evoke love. Eating ice all year round, bathing everywhere, not understanding the autumn wind, regardless of frost and hail, the life of the common people with bare arms and legs, and sarongs as trousers, is enough to make one optimistic and content, not wanting revolution. These lives in the South Seas, seen from the outside, even though the golden age of rubber and tin mines has long passed, still seem worth cherishing.

X X X X X X X

Returning Home

But if you lift the curtain slightly and take a peek inside, you'll see the blue-faced fangs of those who plunder by force, the sighs of lamentation caused by the economic downturn, the scrambling and squeezing for food and seats, the ugly faces emerging from the intensified market struggles of capitalism, and the escalating oppression of the intruders taking over. Faced with all these signs of future storms, I still acted as a cricket escaping from the crack in the giant's palm, leaping towards the old nest, humming the old tune of Mr. Pengze from 1,500 years ago, "Return, oh return!"

X X X X X X X

My Daughter is Yet to be Married

From Medan, I took the Dutch ship "Ting Nong Po" to Singapore, and then transferred to the "Jin Ma" to Hong Kong, which is truly "proletarian." Due to material limitations, I shared a steerage cabin, which was indeed crowded. Needless to say, everyone was an overseas Chinese returning home without a title. The "Jin Ma" was also a Dutch ship. The voyage from Singapore to Hong Kong is in the Chinese Sea. More than 90 percent of the passengers coming and going are Chinese. Chinese people sailing the Chinese Sea, but unable to take a Chinese ship. Of course, most of the ships in China's inland rivers still fly foreign flags, let alone when they leave the country. A fellow passenger said: "My daughter is still living with her parents, she has not yet married." The passengers in the steerage cabin were naturally mostly the real proletarian class. My berth happened to be next to the ship's railing. The passengers often urinated and defecated by the railing, and the smell was quite appetizing. All day long, the cabin was filled with the cries of children and the shouts of women, complete with musical instruments, gramophones, and hawkers shouting, fully displaying the civilization of a Beijing opera house. These entire five days and nights made you feel as if you were in a bustling metropolis, not feeling the loneliness of being on a boat at all.

X X X X X X X

Memories of Sea Travel

I remember in the winter of 1927, when I traveled from Shanghai to Penang, I took the Japanese mail ship "Hakusan Maru." At that time, it was my first time sailing. The rising and falling waves in front of me reflected the sea view with lines of green that I saw in my childhood paintings. From the snow-covered gateway of the country to the scorching green fields, I felt full of novelty. There was a realistic poem in the boat:

"The cold wind blows me to the hot south, taking off my fur coat and changing into white clothes; the seats are filled with people drinking ice on New Year's Day, and sweat can still be seen on the silk shirt." In the summer of 1930, I took the British ship "Ilingborough" from Penang to Rangoon, passing through the Strait of Malacca and entering the Gulf of Martaban. The ship was like a cradle, and the sea was like a round mirror. The voyage was comfortable, and nothing could be better. In the autumn of 1931, I took the "Hai Xing" ship from Rangoon back to China. The ship was small and full, and there were no extra seats on the ship's rail. Passing through the South China Sea, we happened to encounter a hurricane. It floated like autumn wind shaking leaves, and the passengers were all lying down like stiff silkworms. At that time, I sat quietly on the deck, looking at the sea level and the sky, and it was quite interesting. In the winter of that year, I took the German mail ship "Goblen" to Sumatra, passing through Manila, Hong Kong, Singapore, and arriving directly at Teluk Nibung. During the dozen days at sea, the music played on time by the waiter who also served as a band member, and the fox dance performed on the deck by two Italian girls and two red-haired boys with bare legs, still vaguely remained in my mind.

The sales markets for mung beans are mainly Yantai in North China and Minyue in South China. The mainland and this street can also account for one-fourth of the sales volume. Now it is also affected by the Fujian incident. The so-called small foreign merchants in Xiaoluson, etc., mainly purchase high vegetable mung beans, but they cannot be linked. It is now heard that there are still three or four thousand bags in inventory.

It was entirely due to the effect of opinions. The later market may recover slightly, which is also unknown.

Free Talk

About Chen Meigong 265

— Yin Chuan

Chen Meigong (Jiru) published more than 200 types of "Bao Yan Tang Secret Books" in his life, and his contribution to culture can be said to be not small. And he took these "secret books" very seriously and painstakingly proofread and printed them, saying, "I got ancient books," proofread and paid for copying, proofread again after copying, paid for engraving, proofread again after engraving, paid for printing, and proofread again after printing, "but there are still two or three mistakes." (Yanqi You Shi) The difficulty of proofreading and Meigong's meticulousness can be seen from this. According to his books, this man's life was probably quite leisurely. In summer, when he had nothing to do, he edited ancient stories about dispelling summer heat into the "Xiaoxia Bu"; in winter, when he had nothing to do, he edited old stories about dispelling cold during the stove to create "Pi Han Bu." When he got malaria, he delved into ancient books and collected tiger stories in order to ward off malaria, and printed a booklet of "Hu Hui." It's no wonder that he was proud of himself as a "little fairy" in "Taiping Qinghua." He also wrote many books himself, and had a great influence on the development of prose in the late Ming Dynasty. According to the "Bao Yan Tang Secret Book," there were 15 kinds of notes, with 47 volumes; and the "Siku Quanshu Zongmu" (Complete Library in Four Sections) recorded even more than this number. In addition to those related to history, anecdotes, records of events, and records of people, his notes are mostly clear and beautiful, and are "fresh essays" as Mr. Yu Dafu said. Such as a section in "Kuang Fu Zhi Yan" (Words of a Madman):

Suo Kai Fu's poem says: "For you, vulgar people are dressed, and true interests should be lacking." Lu Wenjing's poem says: "Heavenly Flower Temple on Lake Hejia, every window faces the water; no need to close the door to guard against vulgar guests, how many people love idleness?" When I opened the door in the mountains, I used Suo's poem to thank the guests; when the guests came, I used Lu's poem to comfort myself.

Although it is an article that seems like a "small display", a few words have already reflected the life trend of a pastoral poet. This man loved mountain life extremely, and he lived that way. The reason why he could live like this was probably because his life was very affluent. So, he had money to buy books, money to print books, and he lived in the mountains without any worries. In "Yanqi You Shi" (Secluded Affairs of Rock Dwelling), Meigong has two sections writing about mountain birds and mountain neighbors: Mountain birds often start five times at five watch, called reporting the watch, which is the true sound of the mountains. I remember living under Little Kunshan in the past, when the plum rain had just cleared, and the guests were flying goblets. They happened to hear the court, and asked to drink in moderation, so they inscribed a couplet saying: "Flower branches send off guests, frogs urge drums; bamboo sound is noisy in the forest, birds report the watch", which can be called a true record of mountain history.

I once passed a mountain neighbor who was old and loved flowers. Red and purple reflected the house, and he was playing with his grandchildren under the sun. People no longer knew the hustle and bustle of city residence and carriages, let alone the dusty evils of the capital. I gave him a poem: "A small door opens under the pine, famous medicines are planted around the field in front of the hall, the old man hugs his grandson instead of hugging the jar, just wanting to water the flowers as the mountain rain comes."

Here, one can see how Meigong tasted the secluded fun of mountain life and accepted it with a poetic mood when living in the mountains; at the same time, one can also see Meigong's anti-metropolitan mentality and anti-bureaucratic tendency at that time. There are many such notes, so I won't cite them anymore: However, Meigong's life, thoughts, and fresh essay style can already be overviewed. As for the criticism of this life tendency, I don't want to say anything, leave it to the readers. The main works of Meigong's miscellaneous writings include "Jianwen Lu" (Records of What I Have Seen and Heard), "Taiping Qinghua" (Pure Talk in Peaceful Times), "Kuang Fu Zhi Yan" (Words of a Madman), "Zhenzhu Chuan" (Pearl Boat), and "Du Shu Jing" (Mirror for Reading), several kinds.

Dog 266

— Liao Botan

Mr. Shu's relatives, friends, and neighbors all know that there is a dog in his family, whose name is Senping, which is a very good dog丨Once, and it occupied a corner of the XX pictorial.

Senping's life is really leisurely. Mr. Shu has a share in the things he likes to eat; when Mrs. Shu goes shopping, it will follow behind, shaking and sniffing; Miss Shu's hands, which have been sung by "poets with long hair," will stroke its back; at night, it sleeps on the sofa, and if it's cold, it's covered with velvet; if it's hot, it sleeps in the pavilion surrounded by flowers. If it's happy, it may sleep on the foreign cement railing by the pool.

No one in the Shu family doesn't love it. Although the servants are a little jealous, they really love it.

"It's so smart! It's so agile!" In the garden, Miss Shu throws a glove, and it immediately picks it up and runs to Miss Shu's side like flying, standing side by side, isn't the tail wagging enough? Throw it immediately, run immediately, you just throw it, he just runs; when you are tired of it, it may not be tired; whether it is deliberately pretending not to be tired, that is beyond my knowledge.

Once, a thief broke into the Shu family, just when it was late at night and quiet. Who said this was not a good opportunity to be a thief? But it was caught! Strange, isn't it? It turned out to be all Senping's strength!

Because of this, each of the Shu family's servants was severely reprimanded: "What do I raise you for? I raise you to eat! Do you want my meals to turn into mold? If it weren't for my Senping, it would be ruined! It's a waste of people growing so big, not as good as a beast! If you are still so careless in the future, you will be greeting your dog ribs!"

"The master didn't tell us to work the night shift." Sun Han said. Pa pa pa... "Dare you argue with me?"... Pa pa...

Really, this kid has no sense of propriety! The rest of the servants all said it was good to beat him.

Last year, a friend of Mr. Shu, Mr. Mo, announced a lucrative errand somewhere. Mr. Mo also loved Senping. Mr. Shu hurriedly cut his love and personally sent Senping to please Mr. Mo.

But Mr. Mo said coldly: "Thank you! Thank you!" He insisted on not wanting it.

Mr. Shu saw that Mr. Mo really didn't want it. He had no choice but to bring it back! After careful consideration, he quickly sealed hundreds of "travel expenses" and sent them over, and Mr. Mo accepted them. Of course, he also went through the process of declining! Only then did Mr. Shu understand that dogs are ultimately not as good as lace, and it paved the way for Senping's subsequent appearance under the table.

One day, the Shu ladies were having lunch, and a meat bone fell from the table. Originally, Senping would not eat bones, but now, it had to make do with it.

Suddenly, with a "Xiao" sound, a pair of black leather shoes started, and Senping fell beside Miss Shu's legs; Miss Shu laughed and kicked it, and it fell beside the sister-in-law's legs; when Senping knew it was bad, all sixteen feet moved! Help! "Xiao Xiao..." The more it cried, the more "It's so fun!" It finally managed to "break out."

But Defu, the one who added rice next to him, also wanted to join in the fun and win some laughter, so he quickly showed off his skills, chasing from the front of the house to the back, from the back of the house, the back chasing to the front, still Mrs. Shu couldn't bear to watch and stopped him.

Miss丨 laughs! Madam丨 laughs丨 Everyone丨 laughs! Laugh laugh...

"Xiao Xiao Xiao..."

After that, Senping became thinner day by day... and fell ill. "If we don't drive it out, we are afraid of catching cholera?" said the foreign student, the fourth young master. What happened to Senping afterwards? Heaven knows!

Sail 267

— Written by Lermontov, translated by Mu Mutian

A lonely sail in the blue sea fog gleams white... What does it seek in that distant land? What has it left behind in its homeland? The waves rage, the wind howls, the masts bend, creak, and lament. Ah! It is not pursuing happiness. Nor is it running away for happiness. Looking down, the water is brighter than the blue sky, and above is the golden sunlight, but for the traitor, it hopes for a storm, as if there is peace only in the storm.

Another Discussion on the Provocative Nature of Literature by Tang Tao 268

Another stab, and the "target" is still me. This is a bit beyond "coincidence." But of course, it's well-intentioned, supposedly to "remind" me; damn, why should I "make a fuss"?

But good intentions alone might not be enough. The issue, I hear, is "whether there are authors who only want to provoke youth with lies." It sounds as if I don't acknowledge that there are people who lie and deceive. Perhaps this is what they call "a point I've overlooked," which should be "reminded" to me. But in my essay, "The Needs of Youth," I remember having written these sentences:

"Moreover, many recent predecessors are using new things to replace red and blue mandarin hats as tools for seduction and deception, drawing young people into their bags one by one, teaching them to worship, teaching them to shout slogans. After using them, they arbitrarily play with them, mock them, and ridicule them.

"There are also those who disregard the needs of the times, molding young people into figures like themselves, moving them with sweet words, tempting them with great profits. Some become Westernized, others become nationalized. Once they themselves are lifted to the clouds, they trample on the young people beneath their feet one by one."

I clearly acknowledge that there are predecessors who lie and deceive young people, which is why I found it strange that anyone would consider lies as a "need of youth." However, the essayist is intent on "reminding" me, so they erased the aforementioned words and insisted on treating me as if I had "overlooked this point." Now (actually, a long time ago), I can "address this point."

As for "provoking youth," I have never, and will never, treat provocation as a crime to slander others with. I wrote "The Provocative Nature of Literature" to show that provocation is provocation, and lies are lies, and the two should not be confused. But the essayist insists that provocation is lying, and hates that I haven't condemned provocation harshly enough. Thus, this is also "a point I've overlooked."

Actually, there was no need for this regret. Because it's already in the essayist's famous piece. First, lies are equated with provocation, and then it is asserted that provocation must use false emotions. (Are there also false emotions in a famous piece without provocation [?]?) Therefore, this is deceiving youth (?), therefore, this is unacceptable (?), therefore, it is severely condemned. But this time, they deny ever having troubled provocation. And me? I shouldn't "be indignant" nor should I "exert myself."

Conversely, being "too concise" is also not good.

Thighs must be snowy white, and breasts must quiver. Not only is there no suspicion of anesthetizing youth, but it's probably also greatly beneficial to youth. Isn't it?

Correction 269

Yesterday, in the article "Literary Discussions," the original text at the end was: "...Dr. Hu's recent actions, in the eyes of those with a 'historical obsession and textual research obsession,' are not at all surprising." The last name was omitted. We hereby make this correction.

Two Brothers (37) 270

— By Enger Poulsen, Translated by Li Weike

The Dutchman told him how four important coffee shops in the city were willing to give him publicity, and that two local newspapers had agreed to run his advertisements, as long as he sent the editors some medicine.

After a long silence, Malosco asked his brother Jeanne whether he had definitively received the inheritance. He then asked two or three vague questions about the matter. His suspicious concern for Pierre made him resent the donor's partiality. And Pierre thought he understood what he was thinking and guessing, that in that shifting gaze and hesitant tone, he heard the words that were on his lips but unsaid. Words that he would never utter, because he was so cautious, so timid, so cunning.

He no longer doubted it. The old man was thinking, "You shouldn't have let him accept this inheritance. It will damage your mother's reputation." He even thought that Jeanne might be Marisa's son. He must think that! How could he not think that, since it appeared so real, so possible, so obvious? Hadn't Pierre been struggling for three days with all his strength, with all his meticulous thoughts, trying to deceive his own reason, trying to overcome this terrible doubt? Suddenly, he needed to think, to discuss, to boldly and courageously examine this seemingly possible and absurd thing all by himself, so urgently. Without even drinking his glass of raspberry wine, he stood up, shook hands with the very surprised pharmacist, and disappeared again into the fog on the street.

He thought to himself, "Why did Marisa leave all his property to Jeanne?"

It was no longer jealousy that drove him to pursue this matter. It was no longer that slightly base, natural envy that he had been trying to restrain for three days. It was the fear of an inappropriate matter, the fear of even believing that his brother Jeanne was this man's son.

No, he didn't believe it. He couldn't even bring himself to ask this criminal question. But the slight, impossible doubt in his heart had to be completely and definitively cast away. He had to understand this matter thoroughly and be certain of it. He had to have absolute security in his heart, because he only loved his mother in this world.

As he wandered alone in the dark night, he wanted to conduct a detailed investigation in his memory, in his reason, from which he could obtain the shining truth. Then it would all be over. He would never think about it again. He could go to sleep in peace.

He thought, "Come, let's first examine the facts. Then I will recall everything I know about him, his attitude towards my brother and me. I can search for all the reasons why he developed this partiality... He saw Jeanne born? Yes, but he knew me first. If he had a silent and cautious opinion of my mother, then he should have liked me more, because thanks to me, thanks to my scarlet fever, he became a close friend of my parents. So, logically speaking, when he watched my brother grow up, unless he felt an attraction, an instinctive preference for him, he should have chosen me and been more passionate towards me."

Dissenting Opinion on the Suspension of the Nobel Peace Prize 271

— Wei Ba

Nobel, who started by inventing dynamite, in order to repent for the evils he had created during his lifetime, left a will after his death to have all his property organized into a custodial committee to establish prizes for physics, chemistry, and literature. Each year, the committee selects individuals from around the world who have contributed to these sciences and awards them. Among these is a "Peace Prize," which he specifically designated to be awarded to individuals who have contributed to the world peace movement, to atone for his creation of deadly weapons. Past winners, such as Wilson and Briand, were all important figures on the international political stage, famous for supporting peace.

It was rumored that this year's prize might be awarded to Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov, for concluding "non-aggression treaties" everywhere. But according to a recent Havas News Agency dispatch, the Nobel Prize Committee has decided to "suspend the award" for this year's "Peace Prize." Newspaper headlines even used phrases like "A Sign of a World Without Peace" (see the newspaper dated the 16th of this month). To those who care about world peace, especially the Chinese people who are infused with a love of peace, this is an jarring piece of news!

It is undeniable that European, American, and Far Eastern countries are actively preparing for war, but it is not true that the entire world of 1.6 billion people has no one who wants to preserve the word "peace" just because of the bellicose nature of a few powerful countries.

I won't mention others here. Just speaking of our esteemed Republic of China's former Deputy Commander-in-Chief of the Army, Navy, and Air Force, General Zhang, is enough to qualify for a hundred Peace Prizes. Ask anyone, past peace talks were nothing more than signing a document and stipulating a few treaties, becoming nothing more than empty talk on paper. How could it be like our young master's "plan to safeguard peace in the Far East," single-handedly presenting the land of the four northeastern provinces? Although he is now traveling overseas, his contribution is international and even more substantial than the "Pan-European Alliance," etc. of the Briand generation, and should not be obscured. If the representative of the non-resistance policy of "give him whatever he wants" cannot win the reputation of peace and a small prize, then the word "peace" should be permanently removed from dictionaries. Therefore, I specifically raise an objection. This year's Peace Prize should be awarded to our young marshal to boost his morale and dispel all doubts.

(I would like to add that this is of course one of the "international" public opinions and is definitely not because I am also Chinese and hold a feeling of "sharing in the honor.")

Good Neighbor 272

— Yi Qin

My neighbor recently installed a radio, so my ears have also benefited, spending days and nights amidst the noise disturbances.

Now, let me talk about the "gospel" that flies from outside the wall every morning and evening.

In the morning. When you are still asleep in your quilt, you hear the "Diamond Sutra." The sound of the wooden fish, coming through the impenetrable cracks in the wall, goes straight to your pillow. Sometimes it is one person chanting in a drawn-out voice, sometimes it is a chorus of voices making a racket, plus bells, drums, cymbals, making your head spin, and you don't know how many bald monks are messing around at whose radio station. And the time is particularly long, continuing for about an hour, forcing you to get up. After the sutras are recited, what follows are strangely pitched, lifeless "rock-a-bye, baby needs to sleep..."-type baby songs. Songs that make wide-awake people feel discouraged, and confused people just keep sleeping. After about one or two songs, it's already eight or nine o'clock, and I escape from the cage to my place of work. I don't know what they sing after that.

But once evening comes, your ear's good fortune also comes. Because from this time to sleep, the time is longer, so you hear more programs. But when you talk about it in detail, it's also very simple. It's Peking opera, Shanghai opera, Shanghai opera, Peking opera, weeping for Wonderful Root Uncle, weeping for Sun Yat-sen, weeping for Wang Wuneng, etc. The art of weeping is appreciated the most, and it gives me the least good feeling. The next most annoying are the Shanghai opera, which is like the murmurings of a sleep talker, and the Jiangbei tune's "Ah, my Third Brother..." of Capturing Zhang Sanlang as they are about to fall asleep. Peking opera initially gives a sense of clarity for one or two sentences, but if you continue to shout for an hour or half an hour, it will also give you a headache.

So, listening to chanting in the morning and crying in the evening is like taking a class, and I have been in class for more than a week. Although his family hasn't gotten tired of it, I have a bit of a headache.

Logically speaking, since his family turns on the radio, I have no right to listen, but space cannot be separated, so I have to listen as an obligation. Morning and evening are originally the time I write, but now, with such a sad and happy, cymbal and drum-filled racket, I have to put down my pen. There are only two ways to deal with it: one is to dive into the quilt and bury my head to avoid hearing any sound; the other is to run to a friend's house to talk, implementing an escape policy. As a result, both are often used, that is, first going to a friend's house to chat, chatting until late at night before returning to sleep. But time is wasted, it's really "a mute eating coptis, an unspeakable bitterness." Who do I settle this bill of losses with? If this continues, I really have to move.

What I don't understand is how people's hearing can be so different. Mencius said, "The ears are the same in hearing sounds." I'm afraid that's not the truth, is it? Secondly, talking about appreciation, there are so many kinds of sounds, yet they are willing to appreciate chanting and crying. It can really be said to be the ultimate in boredom. This is probably the so-called "Shanghai air"! The radio is a weapon of civilization, the crystallization of science, but it is so abused by the Chinese to spread the most superstitious chanting rituals, it cannot be said to be a strange encounter. I don't know what Marconi, the inventor of the radio, would think if he saw this phenomenon in China in the future, I would like to ask him if I have the opportunity. (End)

"Drizzle" and Others 273

— Li Zhai

Not long ago, the Nanjing Municipal Government issued an order to ban two songs: "Drizzle" and "Sister, I Love You." Then, the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau, following an order from the Municipal Government approving the Ministry of Interior's consultation, banned "supernatural, obscene, and vulgar picture books and paintings," that is, comic strips. Although both of these are considered "trivial matters" by many adults, gentlemen, or modern men and women, they are indeed the current government's "debut" in caring about "public morals" and "popular art." So, regardless of which aspect, it is worth "discussing" it.

The "reason" for the Nanjing Municipal Government to ban "Drizzle" and "Sister, I Love You" was to "maintain public morals." I am not a "loyal comrade" of "Drizzle," so I have no intention of talking nonsense here to "defend" it. However, this ban made me think of two points:

First, "Drizzle" and its kind do indeed have reasons to lose their space and time, but "public morals" is not one of them. Because the meaning, interpretation, and function of so-called "public morals" are all controversial and problematic. What's more, the degree to which certain new nobles or "old heroes" lavish praise on "national opera" and special domestic goods, as well as a large number of men wearing badges and grabbing guns, often gather to watch plays in the Confucius Temple, support "singing stars," and shout praises in strange voices, is more relevant to "public morals" and should be banned more than "Drizzle." So, attacking "Drizzle" with the arrow of "public morals" means that "Drizzle" has no shield to "resist."

Second, before "Drizzle" was born, songs like "Playing Dominoes," "Si Zhou Tunes," and "Meng Jiangnu" had been circulating in many provinces for more than ten years, becoming household names and almost becoming the "national anthem" of the lower-middle class. When "Drizzle" became popular domestically, those songs gradually declined due to "being out of date." But what is "Drizzle?" In terms of rhythm, it is a wearying, decadent sound. If it is true that "song is the voice of the heart," then "Drizzle" is precisely a reflection of the spiritual life of a declining social class that combines "non-resistance" and "national livestock"! In terms of content, it is exactly a self-confession of the soul of a living corpse, ignorant and confused, without any life force. The fact that this kind of song has gained a wide market in China shows that the decadent mood of the leisurely class in China, which is moving further and further away from sunset, is precisely being touched by the heartstrings of our "composers." Leaving aside all the strange theories of "public morals," I believe that before the great era of "Roar, China!" arrives, "Drizzle" and its kind should of course be abandoned in the most easily forgotten places. However, we must never use the "national livestock" method of "eating corn bread or cornmeal is too unsanitary, let's just fast," only passively opposing "Drizzle" and not actively paying attention to creating any substitutes. Therefore, creating and composing a batch of songs with rich content, beautiful form, and sonorous rhythms to replace the decadent sounds of "Drizzle" and its kind is one of the key tasks of today's progressive writers, especially musicians.

We have no objection to the banning of comic strips, but the problem is the same as with "Drizzle": what to replace them with? The "national operas" such as The Peng Gong Case, which are twenty volumes long, The Civet Cat Swaps the Prince, The Investiture of the Gods, etc., the "martial arts classics" such as The True Story of Iron Shirt and The Secret of Zhang Sanfeng's Elixir Refining, the retrograde culture of honoring Confucius and restoring the old order, and the comic strips discussed here... are all based on the ruins of Chinese feudal society. We should not only negatively deny these remnants of feudal culture, but we must also have a positive "effort to pull out the flag and change the banner like Zhao." Otherwise, under the actual needs of the spiritual life of the social masses, simply prohibiting contact with certain paintings or songbooks and not having corresponding things to replace them will result in all prohibitions and inspections becoming empty talk. The constant full houses of various sequential operas and the fact that comic strips do not diminish in popularity due to a single order prohibiting them are clear evidence.

"What's your name?"

"Oh, got it," he found it, "Present, Mr. Liu, allow me to go out to pee, giggle giggle" Another one left. Mr. Liu only turned his head and glanced at him.

There were only a few people left in the classroom; the two girls in front were arguing over a photo of a male classmate. There was also a girl on the left, shy and angry, blushing and rolling her eyes at them. Seven or eight male students in the back were reading newspapers, reading novels, and one was writing a love letter. Some were dozing off. In short, no one was listening to what Mr. Liu was burying his head and talking about.

"Sasha, Sasha!" The minute hand on the watch turned past zero and pointed to the word "six".

"Mr. Liu, let's end the class, there are too few people."

"..." He just ignored it and continued to talk with his head shaking seriously.

"Chichi chi!" The soles of the leather shoes rubbed against the terrazzo floor for a while and finally succeeded, leaving class early.

Eating, Pooping, and Others 276

— Guang Han

Almighty God is only almighty, and is ultimately not perfect enough to be called "perfect." Having created humans, He deliberately arranged for you to have organs and the like, so mortals always have to eat. Because food cannot be completely transformed into blood, eating inevitably leads to pooping. How troublesome! Human life begins with eating and pooping, and ends in a grand finale of eating and pooping!

Humans, to put it grandly, are the masters of the world, conquering everything, dominating everything, and creating everything. To put it modestly, they are just a digestive system that can only manage the function of eating and pooping. The life force is very weak. An earthworm is cut in two, and soon it will turn into two worms, wriggling. Humans, on the other hand, are sometimes hit by half a brick falling from the eaves and immediately "return to the underworld"!

Physiologists tell us that eating and pooping are human instincts, innate, and you can do it as soon as you leave your mother's womb. This gives us a lot of convenience, no need to learn again. It is hateful that God only endows people with the skills of eating and pooping. As for the effort of "getting from poop to mouth," they still have to spend some effort to practice on their own. People are the same, and although there is not much difference in the ability to eat and poop, there are great differences in the means of obtaining food. Some can almost "gain without labor," some must "gain after labor," and some "labor but still find it difficult to gain." Gaining without labor is obviously "getting what one should not get." Gaining after labor is considered "gaining the right way." As for laboring but still finding it difficult to gain, this is undoubtedly "being exploited." Therefore, the world is not fair!

If society had "equal food for everyone" or "less people and more food," that would be great, but things are just the opposite, "more people and less food," that's terrible! Because there are more people and less food, and there is not enough to distribute, there will inevitably be a dispute. The outcome of the dispute is to determine the winner. The winner will naturally have something to eat, and the loser should starve! Who told you not to work hard? Some people will talk a lot about the principles, saying that "survival is a God-given privilege," and everyone should have food to eat. How can you allow you to fight and plunder and make the world what it is? This can only ask "you ask the heavens about this"!

Regarding less food and more people, those who like to stir up trouble speculate that it is either insufficient production or that some strong and barbaric people have snatched too much. Unfounded words are unscientific, and this guess is indeed wrong. Isn't current social production in the middle of an excess, what's insufficient about it? It is also like having a few injustices if it is falsely accused of being seized by people, and it is more appropriate to blame the excessive increase in population.

It is easy to eat, but difficult to get food. This is the scene before our eyes. Since no one has yet provided a good solution, comrades waiting for food can only tighten their belts! Anyway, eating less means pooping less, the gains and losses are offset, why not do it?

In addition to eating, there is also one thing that is equally important, and that is sex. If people have no food to eat, of course, they cannot live. Lacking sexual harmony also makes it difficult to live. As for the function of food and sex, in addition to maintaining the life of individuals and continuing the survival of the race, they also have great help for all cultures. The genes of people creating culture are mostly based on these two behaviors. But from another perspective, the occurrence of various evils in society is nothing more than what is caused by this activity.

Novel

Page 21

is a reflection of the spiritual life of a declining social class that combines "non-resistance" and "national livestock"! In terms of content, it is exactly a self-confession of the soul of a living corpse, ignorant and confused, without any life force. The fact that this kind of song has gained a wide market in China shows that the decadent mood of the leisurely class in China, which is moving further and further away from sunset, is precisely being touched by the heartstrings of our "composers." Leaving aside all the strange theories of "public morals," I believe that before the great era of "Roar, China!" arrives, "Drizzle" and its kind should of course be abandoned in the most easily forgotten places. However, we must never use the "national livestock" method of "eating corn bread or cornmeal is too unsanitary, let's just fast," only passively opposing "Drizzle" and not actively paying attention to creating any substitutes. Therefore, creating and composing a batch of songs with rich content, beautiful form, and sonorous rhythms to replace the decadent sounds of "Drizzle" and its kind is one of the key tasks of today's progressive writers, especially musicians.

We have no objection to the banning of comic strips, but the problem is the same as with "Drizzle": what to replace them with? The "national operas" such as The Peng Gong Case, which are twenty volumes long, The Civet Cat Swaps the Prince, The Investiture of the Gods, etc., the "martial arts classics" such as The True Story of Iron Shirt and The Secret of Zhang Sanfeng's Elixir Refining, the retrograde culture of honoring Confucius and restoring the old order, and the comic strips discussed here... are all based on the ruins of Chinese feudal society. We should not only negatively deny these remnants of feudal culture, but we must also have a positive "effort to pull out the flag and change the banner like Zhao." Otherwise, under the actual needs of the spiritual life of the social masses, simply prohibiting contact with certain paintings or songbooks and not having corresponding things to replace them will result in all prohibitions and inspections becoming empty talk. The constant full houses of various sequential operas and the fact that comic strips do not diminish in popularity due to a single order prohibiting them are clear evidence.

Called Out and Ran 277

— Shi Yang

When the preparatory bell rang, there were only a few students in the classroom. There were quite a few hovering at the classroom door, and I don't know what they were busy with.

"He didn't come!" Old Chen said, standing at the classroom door with a book in his hand.

"He didn't come? Even better."

"No, I just saw him come."

"Anyway, that Mr. Liu rarely calls the roll."

"Mark me present, Old Li..."

"Ding, ding, ding..."

There were still not many students in the classroom. Mr. Liu, wearing glasses with a thousand degrees of nearsightedness, walked onto the podium with a doctoral bag, looked at the students as usual, and took out the roll call list.

"Mr. Liu, don't call the roll, it saves time."

"No, there are very few people today."

Novel

Shanghai 280

— Zhang Lao San

(1) The Stream Under the Bridge

The sound of cuckoos arrived in the spring breeze. I held my younger brother's hand, treading the small path we walked every day, heading towards our parents' graves. The farmers working in the fields always smiled at us, or asked with a rough phrase, "Have you eaten breakfast yet?" After walking along the fields, there was a small bridge. The stream carried fallen flowers under the bridge: flowing from this side to that side, like this every day, like this every year. My younger brother, with light steps, jumped onto the bridge, picked up small pebbles, and threw them into the river. Ripples waved on the water's surface, disappearing slowly with the fallen flowers. To the left of the small bridge was our family's grave. Because it had been in disrepair for years, it was already dilapidated beyond recognition. Looking from the bridge, only a few earthen mounds were visible.

Just as we stepped off the small bridge, it seemed like a shadow flashed past the collapsed gate. In our village, there were often petty thieves stealing pine and cypress trees from people's graves, referring to the magnificent new structures: dark tomb walls, small three- or five-room tile-roofed houses, towering pine and cypress trees, and fresh, new soil. Would petty thieves even notice our grave with only four or five bare, dead pines? I asked my younger brother, and he also saw it, and it seemed like the back view of a woman. We looked around in all directions. Except for the earthen mounds, only a homeless puppy was lying on its back on the grass, waving its limbs at the sun.

In front of the grave, we lay down on the grass, watching the fleeting white clouds. My brother and I did not say a word. Around lunchtime, we retraced our familiar path home, like this every day, like this every year. Although today we lay down on the grass in the same way, there was clearly a different kind of emotion spreading in the silent nature. White clouds flew by, and the sound of cuckoos arrived in the spring breeze. I looked at my younger brother's innocent apple face, looked at the green grass on the two earthen mounds, and clear tears had already moistened my eyelashes. I seemed to apologize for the plan I had made last night, shaking my head. My younger brother also knew that something special was about to happen. He no longer had the lively attitude of jumping onto the small bridge, but neither of us wanted to break the serious atmosphere first. The sun's shadow slowly reached the center. We exchanged knowing glances, stood up, walked across the small bridge, and went home. The stream under the bridge continued to flow endlessly, carrying fallen flowers.

(2) A New Beginning

Stepping out of the school gate, when I breathed in a different kind of air, I once shouted "A New Beginning!" Who would have thought that "A New Beginning" would develop like this! Eating the food I didn't want to eat for more than a year: living the life I didn't want to live for more than a year. Now I am a lonely person in the desert. Where is my way out? Where is what I didn't consider, and couldn't consider? I will do my best, run my course, and find the light I need.

After a day of exhaustion, I still didn't feel sleepy at this time, probably because I was too excited. The passengers on the train were all smiling and having sweet dreams. I envied them. Although everyone didn't know each other's business, when my aunt left, I even promised to go to her house tomorrow. Now I was on a journey hundreds of miles away from my hometown.

When my younger brother woke up and saw the note, I don't know how sad he would be. Returning from the grave, I slightly revealed my intention. My clever younger brother certainly knew that I had a premonition of leaving, but tonight I would leave without saying goodbye. I remembered when my father was dying, he held my hand and told me that I could never leave my younger brother. Father initially loved my stepmother, and my brother and I had long forgotten that we were the sons of his first wife. In his sickly and desolate years, he repented to the portrait of my mother. Father was still our father. Now I have betrayed his dying words. I am an unfilial son to my father and an unrighteous brother to my younger brother. Complex thoughts and the rumbling of the rails played together. I finally cried. I left my parents' grave, left my younger brother whom I could never leave, and I was fighting for a vague future, but the whistle was roaring. It was trying its best to attack the darkness. The curtain of night will unfold a beautiful future before we reach our destination; I will hold my younger brother's hand and atone for my sins before your graves. I occasionally looked up, and the east faintly revealed a milky white color. The beautiful future is right in front of me. I will say again, this is my "New Beginning."

Film Special

A Woman Who Dares to Speak Fairly (Part 1) 281

— Fu

She said that the main reason for divorce lies with women. Of course, this is what men dare not say.

This is what Helen Twelvetrees said. I dare not be so presumptuous, because I am a man. (Some say that if you are so timid, you are not a man, but many men dare not say it, so are they all not men?) Helen said: "Now that divorce is so prevalent in Hollywood, women are the biggest cause of this fashionable divorce disease. What is the reason? It's because when women marry men, they are too casual and don't take it seriously." Helen's words probably come from her own experience, because she has been married and divorced; but now that she has married Frank Wood, she has understood the necessities of a happy family. She said: "If a woman is not prepared to fulfill her responsibilities as a wife, and marries someone rashly, then she is asking for trouble and will have no joy." The following is a discussion published by Helen Twelvetrees:

"The country should issue laws ordering girls' schools to specify home economics as a required subject, so that every girl must learn the principles of being a wife, just as they learn spelling, reading, and arithmetic. When a woman grows up and makes a marriage commitment, she should do so with the same sincerity as choosing a career and signing a contract, or even more sincerity. She should be able to solve various family problems herself, just as she handles various business problems. The reason why marriage has been reduced to child's play now is because most women are not prepared when they step into the church, just as they prepare to do clerical and other duties."

"If I blame women like this, I may be scolded as a traitor to women, but my words are correct. Modern women now walk into marriage with their eyes closed and without thinking. They don't take their marriage vows seriously when they recite them, or they even have a thought in their minds: "If the marriage is not good, I can just get a divorce." The bride of today cannot be called a bride at all, she is just tasting the flavor. Recently, I had a friend. She has been married for less than two years, and recently she wanted to divorce her husband. She said, "I never believed that we could live together for long." She also wanted to sue for alimony. I asked her what the reason for the lawsuit was. She said, "I wasted two years of my time. In these two years, I could have married many people, or I could have made a fortune. So why shouldn't my husband pay a price?" I wouldn't talk to this kind of woman anymore, because she didn't believe that she could live together for a long time, but she married a man and wanted to make some money from him by divorcing him. There is no point in talking about marriage at all. The woman I'm talking about has not yet formally filed for divorce in court, but a friend told me that she is about to file for divorce, and it can be said that there is no reason at all. If she meets a reasonable judge, he will definitely not award her a penny of alimony." (To be continued)

Film Review

Review of "Golden Harvest" 282

— Ling He

Produced by Paramount. Premiered at the Grand Theater

Under the banner of the Blue Eagle, the American authorities are frantically implementing the so-called recovery movement. We can learn from newspapers that President Roosevelt's instructions attempt to mobilize the whole country for this movement, so it is inevitable that the film department will follow suit and reflect this.

To put it very clearly, this is a film with the theme of rural revitalization. Moreover, it strongly raises a serious social problem on the screen. Speaking of this, we cannot help but be surprised. In American films, we very commonly see the kind of intoxicated "Love you" films, but now we see that they are gradually paying attention to society as well. Moreover, they are using major social issues as the subject matter of the films, which is naturally a progressive phenomenon. Of course, we have also seen some films that reflect political forms, such as "Booze and Women," etc. However, the attitude of touting the current policies is also very obvious. If we were to give an example, then "The White House" would be the best proof.

Furthermore, Paramount is the film company that is most diligently loyal to Roosevelt. When the Guanglu Theater was still open, we watched many very diligent films, in addition to "Eagle Song" and "Roosevelt's Struggle History." Now there is this "Golden Harvest," which maintains a consistent attitude.

For the sake of reviewing the content, it is necessary to briefly narrate the story.

A farmer had two sons. The younger son farmed at home, and the older son did speculative business in Chicago. The older son used all means to manipulate the market, and the price of wheat fell sharply as a result, which resulted in the bankruptcy of the rural area. Therefore, the farmers were in distress and went on strike, and the younger son was the leader of the farmers' organization. Later, the older son, due to the interests of his brothers, intended to restore the price of the wheat market. In the end, the older son went bankrupt due to the opening of wheat and returned to the countryside.

As stated in the story, the author certainly stated that the reason for the bankruptcy of the rural area was due to the low market price of wheat, and the reason for the low market price was the manipulation of speculators. Of course, we do not deny that what is pointed out here is quite correct. In the American countryside with rationalized production, the "cheap grain hurts farmers" was not an indirect cause of the collapse. But why did the price of wheat fall? Naturally, the manipulation of the market by speculators is one of the reasons, but from the overall perspective, we cannot ignore the global economic panic. Due to the contradictions of the economic organization, on the one hand, there is overproduction, and on the other hand, purchasing power is reduced. The current world situation is urgent, expanding armaments and preparing for the redivision of the colonial market. Isn't this sharp expression enough to explain the true cause of rural bankruptcy? Of course, this point cannot be explained clearly in a few words, and economists can write a long article on it.

As mentioned above, the author of "Golden Harvest" only explaining the manipulation of the exchange is not enough. At the same time, rural revitalization is not so simple either. Even if speculators do not monopolize the market, they cannot raise the price of the entire wheat, which is just a hopeless fantasy, let alone that speculators will not leave their own interests and discover their conscience to revitalize the rural area, no matter how earnestly the author says that businessmen and farmers should be like brothers. As for the author teaching the merchants from the countryside to return to the countryside in a preaching tone, it is even more laughable. It is simply impossible to justify itself.

As mentioned earlier, American authors are cautiously paying attention to social issues. Regardless of whether they can find a fundamental solution to these problems, it is very gratifying to bring the film into contact with real social phenomena. Because the author handles this kind of subject matter very cautiously, I have also written more about the content. Now let's turn to the performance. Then the author Ralph Murrhy's very solemn attitude is the characteristic of this work. He takes the rural problem as the focus of the work. For the style of general American films, he also writes some unimportant love, which is quite effective in improving the audience's interest. In addition, let's find a few more points to explain the director's cleverness.

1. In order to maintain social order, the scenes of farmers' strikes or riots are not directly depicted, but only indirectly brought through newspaper or telegraph reports.

2. At the beginning, the sketches of the countryside are handled very well with the Disosve method. In particular, the farming scene explains the rationalization of rural production, which is completely different from the Chinese countryside.

3. When the elder son flew to the countryside, many cattle and horses were frightened and ran away, and the old farmer's surprised face was added.

4. The reunion sound when the cups and plates are in a mess, utilizing the characteristics of sound films.

5. The two climaxes in the exchange are both handled properly. 6. When the old farmer got married, the pastor asked the bride and groom to kiss. In our imagination, it must be very embarrassing, but the director made her very brave, beyond people's expectations, and made people laugh.

7. The wrestling scene is very beautiful, and it also says that the two brothers are evenly matched.

The above are the highlights of this film. Generally speaking, the director is full of creativity. As for the actors, there is not much effort needed. Li Que Aaron seems to be more suitable than in previous works. It is better to have him play a strong role after all. Chester Morris, who plays the eldest son, played very well in a few scenes, such as spreading rumors that it was raining and running to the exchange in a raincoat, and when he went bankrupt. The old farmer couple were best when they eavesdropped on others talking at the door. In addition, the two daughters-in-law did not see anything special because the roles were not important.

"Lucky Land" to be Released Soon 283

Chen Yumei chose "Tian Er Lucky Land," which is the news published in various newspapers before. However, is this "Lucky Land" a "Lion Land" or a "Tiger Land"? Of course, you have to see it to know, and even the feng shui master has to see it before he can determine whether it is auspicious or inauspicious! It is said that this "Lucky Land" of Tianyi can be exhibited at the Carlton Theater in early next month for people to visit.

Ziegfeld's Successor After His Death: The Beauty Master Deschall Dai 284

— A Yun

"Greasy Fragrance" is a work of neo-sensualism

Ziegfeld was the "Columbus" who discovered the beauty of the female type. He had sharp eyes and peered into the depths of women's hearts. He made great contributions in the history of film, especially after sound was brought to the screen, which further developed his talent and made many singing and dancing women into stars. When the news of his death was announced, everyone thought that the soul of the Ziegfeld class had fallen, and Ziegfeld's reputation had diminished, but the emerging master Deschall Dai stepped on the path he had not finished and continued his extraordinary efforts; holding up his red-hot torch and being a leader of progress.

He is an artist with a deep understanding of singing and dancing. He has composed music and written many books. His most famous script and song is "A Butterfly Intoxicated by Flowers," which is also his masterpiece of ascending to the peak of art.

Now, he has joined Fox Film Company and is taking on the arduous task of producing. His first blockbuster is "Greasy Fragrance" (according to the film novel "Woman's Weakness" published in this newspaper every day), which is also the masterpiece of Liliang Hawet's first leading role in Hollywood. In order to add to the beauty and atmosphere of the songs, he specially invited his old partners Robin and Fading to help. The two of them are artists who specialize in composing music for Shifrai. As for the director, he immediately took a fancy to David (David's works include the past "Great Gathering of Flowers" and the recent "A Butterfly Intoxicated by Flowers"), and there is also a male lead, Lewis, a warrior from "All Quiet on the Western Front."

He gave a speech saying: In the past, the group of dancers in singing and dancing films were just doing some enthusiastic work. Now that singing and dancing films have re-emerged, the scene is completely different. Every dancer must have a healthy physique, personality, and rich talent. It is not just singing and dancing. Every dancer must have ample opportunities to act and give full play to their instincts. There are countless unknown stars in Jielaiwu who have not been discovered. This new type of singing and dancing film will give every unknown hero (female) a chance to become famous.

Will Hollywood German Stars Return Home? 285

— Donglin

Since Hitler came to power, he has used all means for various domestic and foreign events, and films cannot escape his iron fist. For the sake of reviving German national essence films, Hitler, in addition to setting up a so-called film bank, the first order was to prohibit Jews from setting up photography studios. As a result of this order, film companies established with Jewish capital have closed down one after another. The second order was to summon German film stars abroad to return home: those who violated the order and did not return home would have their German nationality revoked. At present, the German stars in the UK are all preparing to return to Germany. When this news spread to the United States, it caused great panic among the German stars in Hollywood. The famous German star Marie Dailey, and Dorothy Hawk, who gained fame for playing "The Girl in Uniform." I don't know if they will return home? If they don't return to Germany? Their nationality will be gone!

Film Novel Vanilla Beauty (2) 286

— Tian Fu

The economic aggression of imperialism caused the Great China Tobacco Company to suffer a terrible fate.

Business is getting lighter and lighter every day, like a remnant lamp that has run out of oil. There was no way to think about it, so the company authorities decided to make peace with foreign merchants. The terms of the peace treaty are one to five: foreign merchants contribute five boxes, and Great China contributes one box. Even if there is a market, it is not allowed to sell much.

The general manager of Great China signed the contract, his hands trembling. He spoke in a shivering voice: "It's still said...Chinese and foreign industries cooperate, this! ...This is...fair..." He hadn't said the word "fair" yet! He suddenly fainted. This is how the general manager became ill, and he went to the end of his life day by day. At one point, his eyes staring blankly at the important staff of the company surrounding the hospital bed, he gasped and said sadly: "I have worked hard all my life...to create this...Chinese-funded...Chinese-run factory, I never thought...today there would be...such a result..." In a faint sigh, the general manager fell silent.

A dark cloud flew across the sky, and the sun was blocked by the dark cloud.

What a depressing era!

(4) The Justice on the Fist

Foreign tobacco merchants' "fair terms" forced the general manager of Great China to death, and also shattered the rice bowls of countless male and female workers. The company is shrinking day by day, and the number of unemployed people is increasing. Wang Ada's woman has also suffered the fate of being laid off. One night. Ada and his woman and three brothers were sitting around the lamp; the daughter staggered in from outside, her face full of bruises, and cried on the table.

It was the daughter's beauty that caused the trouble again: Lao Hong, the warmonger in the factory, took a fancy to her. When she got off work, he tricked her into playing in the game field. People, bustling and noisy; the sound of gongs and drums was everywhere, all kinds of performances, all kinds of playthings. This country girl encountered something fresh! After coming out of the game field, the daughter was taken to a small inn. After eating, the female companion who came with her gently said to her: "It's late, let's live here!" She smiled and grabbed her hand: "Mr. Hong is very willing to be friends with you! He is a good person, you will definitely not suffer if you are on good terms with him. He has influence in the factory!"

The daughter panicked, her face flushed, her heart pounding: she fled back. She began to recognize the beastly nature beneath the smiling face: she cried.

Ada's brothers gritted their teeth angrily, shaking their fists: "That kid Hong, I'm going to beat that dog thing to death!" He wanted to reason with Hong, but they were caught by a large group of hooligans and "ate tea" in a small teahouse.

Everyone's face was pale, their hats were tilted, and their eyes flickered like inhuman beasts. Wang Ada and his brothers were surrounded in the middle. Wang Ada was so frightened that he kept clasping his hands. "It's all my brother's fault for being young and ignorant, and offending Mr. Hong! Please forgive me, please forgive me!" Thank you for your kindness, and nothing happened: Wang Ada hurriedly paid the tea money. (To be continued)
